    <li> Great battery life, charges quickly, trims very well. A little finicky regarding angles and such, but nothing to get upset about. It could be stronger in thicker hair patches, hence only 4 stars instead of 5.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I would buy this again.</li>
    <li> I&#x27;m a proud owner of this shaver. I use it occasionally to keep my facial hair presentable.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;BUT THAT BATTERY THOUGH. It&#x27;s gotta be lithium. It lasts forever. Admittedly, I only use it once a week, but the battery holds a charge for a very long time. I&#x27;ve charged it like twice over the many months I&#x27;ve owned it. (And unlike Ni-Cad batteries, Lithium  batteries maintain their power output until the end.)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I used this to give myself a buzzcut. That took some effort, but the battery lasted and it looks pretty good.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The shaver does not claim to be water resistant, but I have rinsed the end of it while it was running, without any problems. But always let it dry out before reassembling and storing it, so that rust won&#x27;t form.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cons:&lt;br /&gt;The length dial is slippery when wet. It is hard to turn when my fingers are slippery, and I resort to using my fingernail, since it&#x27;s rubberized.</li>
    <li> After 6 weeks, the battery completely drained and is no longer taking a charge. Of course I can&#x27;t return it now because there&#x27;s only a 30 day return policy.     <li> I&#x27;ve only used this once, but so far so good.  If my past experience with the Remington brand still applies, I&#x27;m sure it will give me years of service.  My last Remington lasted over 6 - 8 years, and I&amp;#34;ve always had good luck with them so far - my favorite brand so I hope I&#x27;m not dissapointed.  Here&#x27;s what I like about this one - My last one had only one blade; I like that this one has the 3 blades because:  1) The stubble blade works great on my head and neck, and it trims much shorter than my last one ever did and this is great for me because I prefer to trim rather than shave those areas, 2) the detail blade makes it much easier to get the details nice and clean, 3) the main blade works well on my beard, and 4) I suspect that the blades will last longer since I&#x27;m using 3 blades, where in the past I only had one blade to do all the work.  Here&#x27;s what I&#x27;m not so fond of:  I had to drop at least one star because it does not have a corded option. I knew this in advance, but the corded options lacked other features that I like, so I made this choice anyway, but why is it so difficult to give us the option?  It&#x27;s really irritating when I start to get ready for work or a night out, and my trimmer dies before the job is done.  If they can&#x27;t provide a corded option, I would at least like to have a gauge so I know I&#x27;m doomed if I don&#x27;t charge it more first.  I think this is something that should be fairly simple: many of my battery operated devices have a visual representation of how much charge is left, so the technology is anything but new.  Come on Remington, give us a cord or a gauge, and this could well be the perfect trimmer for me!</li>

    <li> Ouch.  And blood.  I tried it twice and got the same result both times.  Do not put these blades anywhere near your skin.  They will cut a ragged edge.     <li> I&#x27;ve been using the trimming extension on my electric shaver to shave my face because my skin is sensitive and breaks out/gets ingrown hairs if I shave with the foil or use a razor. I believe that Remington has either designed this cutter with an undersized battery and/or they are using poor quality batteries.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Bottom line . . .  it&#x27;s a good quality cutter but be prepared to buy a new one about every two years. Did some research on Amazon and after reading hundreds of reviews on a dozen trimmers, went for the Remington MB040.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Here&#x27;s what I like:  The height wheel is really nice - at #2 or #3, I get a nice &amp;#34;three day stubble look&amp;#34;.  I use the lowest setting #1 to trim around my mustache and chin area - where the hair tends to get quickly out of control.  The guard also easily removes for precise trimming around the next line and stray hairs in the cheek area.  The battery also lasts a long time.  If I use the trimmer 2 to 3 times per week, I&#x27;m only charging the unit once every couple of weeks.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;My one complaint is that the trimmed hair goes everywhere but I didn&#x27;t want a noisy vacuum attachment, so I knew I would have to deal with a mess after trimming.  I suggest you do the trimming in the shower or in front of the sink with a towel spread on the counter.  Overall, excellent buy and my wife is happy.  Happy wife, happy life.</li>

Pros:  - Long battery life, with less battery drainage. - Includes 3 different blades which is helpful. - Many length settings. - Powerful motor compared to Cruzer 6. - Better trimming in the neck, but needs several passes. - Easy blades removal. - Easy to clean the trimmer. - Good grip, and positioning of blade. When I was using Cruzer 6 the trimmer head wasn&#x27;t easy to use it to do precise trimming. To be more clear, I don&#x27;t have a good view of what I am trimming, the braun cruzer 6 [ Face shaver model ] trimmer head is placed in a weird position that I have a difficult time seeing what I am going to trim. I&#x27;m not saying it is hard, but MB4040 is easier, that&#x27;s all.  I cannot make a professional review, since I am not a hairstylist. I am a person who doesn&#x27;t wan&#x27;t to waste he&#x27;s time at the barber shop. So in order to make my review more helpful I compared it to another beard trimmer.  I will update my review with time.  UPDATE: 3/2/2014  I have tried to use this trimmer for trimming my beard ( not shaving it ) with the guard. When I trimmed my sideburns on level 5 the result was good. BUT, when I trimmed the hair under my lips the result were OK. I Said to myself to push the the trimmer head a little bit, and the hairs were shorter. I thought maybe when I was not pushing it too hard the result wasn&#x27;t accurate, but when I pushed a little bit it trimmed shorter. So, I said why not push more? The result was horrible. Some of the hairs were short, and are gone, some isn&#x27;t equal in height to other hairs! I knew the reason before I started trimming, you wanna know why? Because the trimmer guard is FLIMSY, NOT HARD, ISN&#x27;T ENGINEERLY WILL DESIGNED! So, my recommendation to those people who ( only/main reason ) needs this product for trimming their beard is DON&#x27;T BUY IT. Reason? The guard will not give you a smooth accurate length of hair. As humans we might press strongly in this spot, and press gently in another spot while trimming, right? So, the product will not satisfy you in what you need it to do. As for my needs, this product fulfills them :), and the 5 stars remain :)  If you read this REMINGTON, then please change the guard to a new one, with a rigid structure.  UPDATE: 14/5/2014  My initial review was influenced by my past bad experience with Braun Cruzer 6. So, it was giving you the impression that I am happy about the product, which I was at the beginning. Because I have Braun 790 I wasn&#x27;t paying attention that this product lack the precision, because the shaver cleans the small hairs after it.  So, it&#x27;s down to this:  - Edging sideburns is good, because the hair is usually long, so it&#x27;s easy to edge it. - Edging the mustache is NOT precise if your mustache is not long. I mean if it&#x27;s around 5mm. You would try to edge it multiple times, and you still would not get the perfect result. Because I have Braun 790, it will clean those small hairs, and would give me a better shave around the edges of my mustache. It would look cleaner than before.  Bottom line: - Not great Edging of the mustache, and beard &amp;#34; If your beard or mustache was long u wouldn&#x27;t notice much, but if it was short you would notice &amp;#34; - Great battery, that is the biggest pro in it - This mainly would be good for shaving the entire beard. - Not aimed for a professional shave. Yes, with only this machine, you will not feel that you got the same shave you&#x27;d get at a barber shop.  This is not a good trimmer, but it&#x27;s decent.  If you got the money then consider two companies, Andis &amp; Wahl. They have great trimmers, especially those wired ones. Yes, many would like wireless, but the wired ones have the power to edge, and trim with breeze. Go to YouTube, and see.  I am thinking to go with the Andis T Trimmers &amp;#34; T-Outliner &amp;#34; or &amp;#34; Superliner &amp;#34;. As they edge way better from seeing at YouTube. Till now I don&#x27;t know if they can trim for specific lengths. Still asking. They would cost you extra 20$.  I left only 2 stars, because of the battery. Can&#x27;t say I hate it. It&#x27;s a decent trimmer.  Update: 14/06/2014  So, since using this trimmer for 7 months, it paid for itself, and more! I bought Andis Superliner 4820 Model which supports both 110v + 220v, http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B00791CU6K/ref&#x3D;oh_details_o00_s00_i01?ie&#x3D;UTF8&amp;psc&#x3D;1 It came with attachments: 1/16, 1/8, 1/4, and 3/8. Which exactly what I want. I have a review there that you can check it out :)  Comparing the two trimmers is not fair since they are in a different categories.  But, for letting you know what was the difference between the two, or let&#x27;s say between this and a wired trimmer that is from Andis or wahl, and can be zero gapped: Andis Superliner resolve all the complaints I said about the MB4040. With blade factory setting you can get as close as 0.1mm which will give you great edging, and when you zero gap the blade you would get a more precise edging, or closer shave. Blade cuts with less passes compared to MB4040 Attachments are better because they are rigid plastic not flimsy like MB4040 guard.  Now, I will never think of buying a trimmer. Andis superliner seems that it will serve me for years, will, let&#x27;s hope so :)  Conclusion:  MB4040 I would recommend it for people who travel. Battery, and decent trimming will definitely get the job done until you come back home. Or maybe with the collaboration with another razor you would get a stylish beard &amp; mustache. THIS IS TO THE MANY THAT RATE THIS LOW STARS.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Ok after spending some time reading the low reviews I want to add a few things.&lt;br /&gt;First there are 3 blades with this trimmer. Below I will describe them for further use in this review.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Ok looking at the pictures on this amazon product description page I will refer to the 3rd picture from the top in the description.&lt;br /&gt;So the 3 blades are as follows.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;1. Beard Trimming Blade. (This is the big blade with the wide teeth)&lt;br /&gt;2. Goatee Trimming Blade. (This is the one with the small cutting blade with fine teeth)&lt;br /&gt;3. Stubble Trimming Blade. (This is the one with the same length blade as the Beard Blade but it has finer teeth)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Ok so many users complain that they cut themselves when using this trying to shave their bare skin. So use this guide line.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The Beard Trimming Blade is only supposed to be used with the plastic guide for TRIMMING YOUR BEARD NOT SHAVING YOUR FACE.&lt;br /&gt;I have used the stubble blade on my neck, but I don&#x27;t care for that blade much.&lt;br /&gt;After trimming my beard a little with the Beard Trimming Blade AND THE PLASTIC GUIDE. I then use the GOATEE TRIMMING BLADE TO SHAVE TO MY BARE SKIN, so I use the GOATEE Blade to shave my neck and the edge of my chin strap to keep it styled. And I HAVE NEVER BEEN CUT USING THE GOATEE BLADE I just shave strips under my neck until I am finished. So ONLY USE THE BIG BEARD BLADE WHEN YOU ARE TRIMMING, AND NOT SHAVING YOUR BEARD, AND YOU HAVE TO USE THE GUIDE WITH THIS BLADE. 2. USE THE SMALL GOATEE BLADE FOR ALL OTHER SHAVING THAT INVOLVES SHAVING TO BARE SKIN LIKE UNDER YOUR CHIN AND ON YOUR NECK.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Also there are some general guidelines to use when dealing with lithium ion batteries.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;First don&#x27;t let them drain all the way that can ruin the battery life.&lt;br /&gt;Also don&#x27;t let them sit for a long time without charging doa maintenance charge like once a month.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;can&#x27;t post links but just Google how to charge and maintain lithium ion batteries.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Follow these few rules and you won&#x27;t cut yourself when using this. And at least look into how to safely use and charge lithium ion batteries. Not all things are maintenance free.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;UPDATE 4/27/2016!!!!!!!&lt;br /&gt;I have had this for a little over 2 years now, and have only charged the battery less than 10 times. In fact, I haven&#x27;t even charged it yet this year. I use it about once a week to trim up my beard, and it always works. I have read several bad reviews regarding the battery. Make sure when you buy it to follow the directions and FULLY charge it when you open the package. After that, I only charge it when it is dead or very low, and that seems to do the trick for me. This is the best beard trimmer I have ever used.     <li> Please read the content and understand that it is aimed at the manufacturer rather than the specific device before you flame this review.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Let me first thank Amazon for their generous return policy. They&#x27;re great.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I have no idea how well this product works. I never will. If I had seen a picture of the packaging, I wouldn&#x27;t have ordered it, because it comes in a ridiculously complicated clamshell.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Why am I taking this much time to write a negative review? That&#x27;s the fault of the manufacturer for creating shelf-friendly but user-unfriendly packaging. I never saw it on the shelf, obviously, but I&#x27;m sure the package looked great, with the razor and attachments gleaming through plastic clamshell for passers-by to inspect.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I open dozens of packages like this every year. I don&#x27;t have ham fists or mental impairments that keep me from opening them properly. [Insert flame comment here] I go at things carefully, slitting the tape on the sides and top with a pocketknife and then pulling the inside packaging out.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Let&#x27;s describe this particular one. There are two items loosely fit in plastic at the top of the large clamshell. When removing the clamshell from the packaging, these two things fell out onto the table. (The shaver unit itself, and then the plastic cover with the beard comb attached to it.) Turning the package over reveals the power cords and instruction manual underneath. I then ask myself where the other grooming attachments are. Oh - they&#x27;re still stuck into the top of the package. They&#x27;re underneath another layer of plastic that is stapled to the inner cardboard shell.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Stapled. Interesting. Well, I guess we just pop the staples out since the manufacturer didn&#x27;t include a staple remover.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I use my pocketknife to pry off the staple on the side where the attachments are. The two shaving attachments -- which were more or less stuck to the plastic clamshell that I was trying to pry open -- then fly out of the packaging and onto the floor. Each attachment consists of two blades, one on the front and another on the back that is held in place with a spring and a plastic assembly. Falling to the floor immediately causes them to spring apart, effectively breaking the attachments.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Could I try to put these pieces back together? Probably. Should I have to? No. It&#x27;s the manufacturers fault for creating idiotic packaging that would cause significant damage to necessary parts just by opening the package.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;What&#x27;s wrong with a simple box that has a picture of the item on the cover? I can even deal with clamshell plastic provided it can easily be separated to get at the parts.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Remington - you and others who do this kind of thing need to understand this.</li>

    <li> Remington MB4040 Lithium Ion Powered Men&#x27;s Rechargeable Mustache and Beard Trimmer&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The Remington MB4040 looks, feels, and operates like any other cordless trimmer. The main difference is that the MB4040 has a Li-Ion battery pack and these tend to last a LOT longer than the cheaper and more common Nickel Cadmium batteries.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The titanium coated blades offer long-lasting sharpness, but many of the other cordless trimmers like the ones from Philips, also feature titanium coated blades. The MB4040 does have interchangeable blades designed for a variety of tasks from trimming beards to maintaining goatees, and trimming hair. The blades are easy to change, but they come fairly well oiled which makes cleaning somewhat messy because the oil attracts the hair shavings and requires some scrubbing with soap.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The packaging is total rubbish. The blister pack is stapled to the cardboard, and it made it difficult to remove the trimmer. It does not include any type of storage for the extra blade heads, so I ended up throwing the other blades into a plastic bag.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The included adjustable comb is very innovative and easy to use. A few clicks on the thumb wheel will raise or lower the comb. However, the design of the comb allows it to grab my short hair at times. It is too flexible and should have been made more rigid without the open edges that can grab at hairs.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The charging LED will shut off to indicate a full charge, which is a nice feature. NiCd cordless trimmers and razors tend to keep charging, while the Li-Ion trimmers/razors usually provide a full charge indicator.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall: 4/5 stars, there&#x27;s nothing truly revolutionary about the MB4040. It&#x27;s a convenient cordless trimmer with a Li-Ion battery pack that allows it to perform better for a longer period of time versus the cheaper NiCd trimmers. I don&#x27;t like how the comb can grab at my hair, and there&#x27;s no storage for the extra trimmer heads.</li>

    <li> As a long-time user of beard-trimming devices, I&#x27;ve learned it&#x27;s the emitted sound that reveals their quality. The tone of this one suggests the internals are precision built and that they will last for a long time. The exchangeable blades are a nice touch, especially at this price point. Battery power and life seem leading edge - I am interested to see how this one ages.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;All external pieces with which your hand or face make contact have smoothed/rounded edges, unlike a previous trimmer I endured. The only comfort-related gripe, which overall ranks fairly minor, is the positioning of the on/off switch. It sits very low on the handle, making one handed operation awkward. I felt like I was just about to drop the unit when I turned it off.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;In use, I did experience something that another reviewer mentioned: an occasional single hair that does not get trimmed and the high number of passes required to get consistent length over a specific area. After some examination (and comparison to two other trimmers), I believe the culprit is the wide spacing of the teeth on the adjustable comb. Narrower spacing (as found on the others) forces curlier hairs to straighten. On the Remington, there is room between teeth to allow rogue hairs to remain partially coiled or angled away from the meshing blades. Ooops.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So, in short (sorry), extra time is definitely needed for additional passes to achieve truly even beard length - not ideal. It helps to have a fine (..manual..) comb to assist with the straightening duties. And a third hand for the mirror.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;That adjustable comb is also a bit flimsy. I will be treating it carefully (and making sure to store it at the \\&quot;minimum/No. 1\\&quot; setting) as I don&#x27;t think the attachment  would survive even a single drop onto even a wood (much less tile) floor. Incidentally, setting the adjustment dial to the \\&quot;No. 1\\&quot; setting makes sliding the adjustable comb on or off easier.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The too-wide tooth issue is theonly flaw - but a serious one - on an otherwise excellent product. Three stars, then.</li>

Some were plug-in models and some were battery operated. Some were better than shears and a comb and, as the years, they got better but not perfect. As my Panasonic trimmer, purchased three years ago, was no longer holding a charge, I came to Amazon and started shopping. When I came across these Remington&#x27;s, I read quite a few of the reviews and was intrigued by some of the features. I had owned, it seemed, everything but a Remington brand in the past. The strength of the motor is better than any battery charged unit that I&#x27;ve used previously, the blades much, much sharper. I&#x27;ve only used it three times in the past two weeks, but the first time was on my beard that hadn&#x27;t been trimmed in over four months (long story there) and, after getting rid of all that rubbish, actually getting some shape into what was remaining and using the bare blade to get rid of the stubble so that I could partially shave a bit of my neck and cheek so: and all that in the first go with the device. So far, no more charges needed, and I&#x27;ve used it weekly just to keep things in shape.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Previous beard trimmers have lasted from one use to three years. I&#x27;m betting that this device will outlast that three-year mark. I simply could not be more pleased with the craftsmanship, the ease of use and the results. I hope, however, that I never have to tackle another four-month growth.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;UPDATE 2:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Well - two years and five months have passed and I&#x27;m still using this trimmer, every week or so, and it continues to work splendidly. With so many men&#x27;s grooming devices available now it has become more difficult to choose &#x27;the best&#x27; amongst the many. I will not say that this Remington brand is the very finest of the bunch but, for me, it has proven to work very well. Yes, I made the foolish mistake of using the standard blade directly on my skin and, yes, I had four distinct wounds and a bit of blood gushed from each. I am a stubble-faced now, after 40-years of being the full-beard type, and I have to say that the slight beard is so much cooler in the hot summer months. I am still a very pleased user and certainly recommend this trimmer for any man with the slightest facial hair that needs to be tamed.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This trimmer continues to be the very best that I have owned. Someone (and I don&#x27;t know who) slipped another brand&#x27;s trimmer into my bathroom mirror and I (mistakenly) gave it a whirl: do you wish to see the photos of my toilet-papered face? Well, I&#x27;m not posting any!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Should I run across any trimmer claimng to be better than this Remington or claiming to be better than any trimmer available, then I would certainly try it. I will not say that this Remington brand is the very finest of the bunch but, for me, it has proven to work very well. Yes, I made the foolish mistake of using the standard blade directly on my skin and, yes, I had four distinct wounds and a bit of blood gushed from each. I am a stubble-faced now, after 40-years of being the full-beard type, and I have to say that the slight beard is so much cooler in the hot summer months. I am still a very pleased user and certainly recommend this trimmer for any man with the slightest facial hair that needs to be tamed.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This trimmer continues to be the very best that I have owned.
